  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

              <div id="descriptionmodule" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="descriptionmodule_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>I've always been surprised to see the &lt;defaultSearchField&gt; element and &lt;solrQueryParser defaultOperator="OR"/&gt; defined in the schema.xml file since the first time I saw them. They just seem out of place to me since they are more query parser related than schema related. But not only are they misplaced, I feel they shouldn't exist. For query parsers, we already have a "df" parameter that works just fine, and explicit field references. And the default lucene query operator should stay at OR – if a particular query wants different behavior then use q.op or simply use "OR".</p> 
                  <p>&lt;similarity&gt; Seems like something better placed in solrconfig.xml than in the schema. </p> 
                  <p>In my opinion, defaultSearchField and defaultOperator configuration elements should be deprecated in Solr 3.x and removed in Solr 4. And &lt;similarity&gt; should move to solrconfig.xml. I am willing to do it, provided there is consensus on it of course.</p> 
                 </div> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>

maintainer\\\" i view the defaultSearchField as a fairly important piece of information the schema maintainer is providing for people who then consume the index.  It\'s a statement (from the schema maintainer to any\\/all solr users) that in the absence of any more specific use cases provided by the solr instance maintainer, this field can be used as a field to search on.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIs that conceptual meaning significant enough to warrant saying \\\"this is a crucual feature in solr\\\" ? .. probably not, but it\'s how i think about it.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAt this point though, i\'m not sure that eliminating them really improves anything.  yes we have the df param and the q.op param, but if\\/when those params aren\'t set, these values provide system wide defaults.  We certain \u003cb\u003ecan\u003c\\/b\u003e deprecate them, but i don\'t know that that really helps our users in anyway.  we could move them to solrconfig.xml, but that would require the same amount of work from users to modify configs as just eliminating them.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003ei guess what i would propose is that since the only real issue with them is potential confusion about where\\/why they exist, we:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eleave the code in to use them as fall back defaults\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eleave tests in place to sanity check that they work\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003estop advertising them in the examples\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n...ie: quietly deprecate in 3x, but don\'t explicitly remove in 4x.  \u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cblockquote\u003e\u003cp\u003eAnd &lt;similarity&gt; should move to solrconfig.xml. This isn\'t quite breaking things but close enough IMO.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eMy reasoning is that there are lots of people running with pre 3.6 Solr. If I were them, I would be pretty annoyed if I got a point release, moved my &lt;fieldType&gt; and &lt;field&gt; and &lt;copyField&gt; definitions over to a new example schema, started up my system and had it behave differently because the &lt;defaultField&gt; was quietly removed.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThis is one of those issues that, while it may well be technically preferred, making this change is making decisions that affect running systems to no benefit of people \u003cem\u003ealready\u003c\\/em\u003e running those systems. \\\"First do no harm\\\" comes to mind.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eYes, all my objections can be met with \\\"but all they have to do is make sure that they put &lt;defaultField&gt; back\\\". But that\'s not the point. We shouldn\'t make gratuitous changes that make life harder for people trying to upgrade a point release.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eGoing to trunk is another matter, it will require a significant effort (reindexing comes to mind) and users will approach that with much more care than 3.5 -&gt; 3.6.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eFWIW\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nErick\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"erickerickson\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_13236884_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=erickerickson\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"erickerickson\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Erick Erickson\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_13236884_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'23\\/Mar\\/12 18:25\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2012-03-23T18:25:16+0000\'\u003e23\\/Mar\\/12 18:25\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    deprecate in 3x OK. Remove from 3x examples very much NOT OK. Add a note in the 3.x schema that this is no longer preferred, sure. But leave it in. \\n\\n Remove them from trunk schema.xml OK. Remove support from 4x NOT OK. Our policy is generally to be back-compat through one major release. This isn\'t quite breaking things but close enough IMO. \\n\\n My reasoning is that there are lots of people running with pre 3.6 Solr. If I were them, I would be pretty annoyed if I got a point release, moved my &lt;fieldType&gt; and &lt;field&gt; and &lt;copyField&gt; definitions over to a new example schema, started up my system and had it behave differently because the &lt;defaultField&gt; was quietly removed. \\n\\n This is one of those issues that, while it may well be technically preferred, making this change is making decisions that affect running systems to no benefit of people  already  running those systems. \\\"First do no harm\\\" comes to mind. \\n\\n Yes, all my objections can be met with \\\"but all they have to do is make sure that they put &lt;defaultField&gt; back\\\". But that\'s not the point. We shouldn\'t make gratuitous changes that make life harder for people trying to upgrade a point release. \\n\\n Going to trunk is another matter, it will require a significant effort (reindexing comes to mind) and users will approach that with much more care than 3.5 -&gt; 3.6. \\n\\n FWIW \\nErick              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eBernd:\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nSupport for a default search field name still exists mostly for compatibility, and in perhaps some peoples\' views as a matter of preference.  It wasn\'t actually required before its deprecation.  I thought it was only the fallback for parsing a lucene query but you indeed point out dismax has it as a fallback for \'qf\', and it\'s used by the highligher as a fallback for  \'hl.fl\' although it appears the highlighter consults \'df\' too.  The main point behind its deprecation is that I think you should be explicit in a request which field(s) apply to what query strings or other features because the schema (schema.xml) can\'t know.  The same applies to the default query operator which is even more of an odd duck sitting in schema.xml.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eBernd, simply define \\\"qf\\\" in your request handler definition to make Solr respond correctly to the same queries you had before.
